  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a6e833bf-4450-45bd-b818-e95fa7e7788e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer18010825348653045092">Wilhelmina has a hundred identities.<br/><br/><i>She is a princess.</i> When the Indigo Kingdom conquered her homeland, Wilhelmina and other orphaned children of nobility were taken to Skyvale, the Indigo Kingdom’s capital.   <span id="freeText18010825348653045092" style="display:none">Wilhelmina has a hundred identities.<br /><br /><i>She is a princess.</i> When the Indigo Kingdom conquered her homeland, Wilhelmina and other orphaned children of nobility were taken to Skyvale, the Indigo Kingdom’s capital. Ten years later, they are the Ospreys, experts at stealth and theft. With them, Wilhelmina means to take back her throne.<br /><br /><i>She is a spy.</i> Wil and her best friend, Melanie, infiltrate Skyvale Palace to study their foes. They assume the identities of nobles from a wraith-fallen kingdom, but enemies fill the palace, and Melanie’s behavior grows suspicious. With Osprey missions becoming increasingly dangerous and their leader more unstable, Wil can’t trust anyone.<br /><br /><i>She is a threat.</i> Wraith is the toxic by-product of magic, and for a century using magic has been forbidden. Still the wraith pours across the continent, reshaping the land and animals into fresh horrors. Soon it will reach the Indigo Kingdom. Wilhelmina’s magic might be the key to stopping the wraith, but if the vigilante Black Knife discovers Wil’s magic, she will vanish like all the others.<br /><br />Jodi Meadows introduces a vivid new fantasy full of intrigue, romance, dangerous magic, and one girl’s battle to reclaim her place in the world.</span>

    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/931263659?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer931263659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4920773616790889276">In 1211, Genghis Khan's tiny army of 2,000 was vastly outnumbered by the Jin army, 500,000 strong. The week before the battle, the entire Jin army got food poisoning (they were trying to do a cleanse before the big day by eating more probiotics, as it turned out, not all things were meant to be fermented, least of all, pork). Suffering from bouts of severe diarrhea, the Jin army fled (leaving behind unspeakable trails of...unmentionable things), resulting in a decisive victory for Khan(h...just </span>
  <span id="freeText4920773616790889276" style="display:none">In 1211, Genghis Khan's tiny army of 2,000 was vastly outnumbered by the Jin army, 500,000 strong. The week before the battle, the entire Jin army got food poisoning (they were trying to do a cleanse before the big day by eating more probiotics, as it turned out, not all things were meant to be fermented, least of all, pork). Suffering from bouts of severe diarrhea, the Jin army fled (leaving behind unspeakable trails of...unmentionable things), resulting in a decisive victory for Khan(h...just kidding). Genghis Khan went on to conquer most of Asia and Europe.<br /><br />In 1942, Jackson Pollock got dumped by his girlfriend. "You're just, like, so <i>boring</i>," she said. "Why do you have to paint butterflies and kittens all the time?" A devastated Pollock spent the night drinking. In the morning, the wealthy art patron Peggy Guggenheim arrived. They had arranged a meeting for her to review his art. She came into the studio to find an entire studio of canvases with paint splattered haphazardly all over them. In his drunken state, Pollock had destroyed his canvases. "Brilliant!" Guggenheim exclaimed. "This is revolutionary, I've never seen anything like it!"<br /><br />"Uh, yeah, I had a...vision" Pollock muttered. "Totally meant to do that." Pollock went on to become one of the most well-known artists of the 20th century.<br /><br />In 1796, Edward Jenner was fucking a milkmaid in the barn. His wife burst into the barn. "EDDIE, WHAT THE FUCK?!" she screeched. Edward quickly scrambled to his feet, "I'm doing this...for science!" he stuttered. "I'm, uh, trying to do an experiment! See? Look at this...cow! I was just trying to see if the...err, stuff...from...that cow could cure her...vag---po---cow pox! Yeah! That's it!"<br /><br />"With your pants down?!" she screamed. "Don't question the methods of science!" he retorted.<br /><br />Edward Jenner went on to become the father of modern vaccines, his first invention the vaccination for smallpox.<br /><br /><b>In case you didn't know, those stories were all bullshit, wrenched from the depths of my demented imagination.</b> Naturally, all of those historical figures were brilliant ones, revolutionary strategist, artist, scientist. They worked hard, it took time for them to develop their skill and methodology.<br /><br />The point is that their accomplishments would have held so much less meaning if they had stumbled across them through no effort of their own, if their achievements were pure, dumb luck.<br /><br />In books, I want characters who are admirable, who succeed through sheer brilliance and plotting. I don't want the use of <b>deus ex machina</b> and chance to result in WIN. <br /><br />And that's exactly how the characters in this book succeed: sheer good fortune, the complete idiocy of everyone else. The main characters <b>essentially danced their way down Easy Street.</b><br /><br />Want to infiltrate a kingdom and get close to its royalty? Just pretend you're a duchess from a foreign land. Sure, nobody will doubt you at all. Indeed, they don't. <blockquote>
  <i>“Lady Julianna, Lady Melanie, you’re both welcome in Skyvale Palace for as long as you’d like to stay. Our home is your home.”</i>
</blockquote>Easy as pie.<br /><br /><b>Want a top-secret map?</b><blockquote>
  <i>“A map. I want to know which windows lead to which rooms. I want to know where the armories are, where guards are stationed, and even where King Terrell sleeps at night. I want to know everything about that place."</i>
</blockquote>Your enemies will <b>literally hand it to you.</b><blockquote>
  <i>“The Indigo Kingdom is so kind to us. Whatever we require for our reclaiming of Aecor will be provided.”</i>
</blockquote>Need to locate a secret map? It's <b>literally marked down for you.</b><blockquote>
  <i>“On my way out, I glanced again at the wall map, and the mysterious scribbles on the western border of Liadia.<br />They read confidential and debated.”</i>
</blockquote>Like, are you fucking kidding me?<br /><br />I like books with admirable heroes and heroines. I like to see them succeed through skill, intelligence, and effort. This book has no merit. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4920773616790889276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1230263958" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1230263958" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1230263958?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1230263958" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14056837724402262886"><strong>… Is that it?</strong> Is that all this book had to deliver? I am feeling more than underwhelmed by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18081228.The_Orphan_Queen__The_Orphan_Queen___1_' title='The Orphan Queen (The Orphan Queen, #1) by Jodi Meadows' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Orphan Queen</a> right now.<br/><br/>It was a complete disappointment. From start to finish. As a matter of fact, the only thing I found myself appreciating was the writing. Pretty and well fit to a fantasy story, it might have been the only thing that kept me on reading.<br/><br/>There was nothing I actually ‘‘hated’’ but it is rare for me to ‘‘hate’’ something inside a book, unless a character, scene, relationship, world-bu</span>
  <span id="freeText14056837724402262886" style="display:none"><strong>… Is that it?</strong> Is that all this book had to deliver? I am feeling more than underwhelmed by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18081228.The_Orphan_Queen__The_Orphan_Queen___1_" title="The Orphan Queen (The Orphan Queen, #1) by Jodi Meadows" rel="nofollow noopener">The Orphan Queen</a> right now.<br /><br />It was a complete disappointment. From start to finish. As a matter of fact, the only thing I found myself appreciating was the writing. Pretty and well fit to a fantasy story, it might have been the only thing that kept me on reading.<br /><br />There was nothing I actually ‘‘hated’’ but it is rare for me to ‘‘hate’’ something inside a book, unless a character, scene, relationship, world-building or any other relatively important element inside a story is frustrating or peeving enough for myself to not being able to handle it.<br /><br />This was just completely <strong>boring and unsurprising</strong>. I had been curious about the infiltrating a palace happening and the magic, verily, but even the balls and the activity at court sparkled no interest in my eyes, as it usually does. And princes… I usually cannot resist them, but Tobiah – dull, monotonous and phony Tobiah – didn’t even <strong>TRY</strong> to make us like him. I strongly hoped for him to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[not be the one disguised as Black Knife but, well, it was to be predicted <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />Surely, when you do not feel any affinity for the main character of a story, it is pretty difficult to take full enjoyment in it. Wil was your typical fantasy heroine – ready to fight, rash by moments and always fixed on a certain goal to achieve. Not that this is a bad thing – of course not. But there was nothing noteworthy about her… nothing that would make her standing out in a crowd of determined girls. She sure had qualities that I can admire in my general fierce heroine but too much of the same becomes… <strong>unstimulating</strong>.<br /><br />Perhaps the whole masked-vigilante-with-a-fancy-name-watching-over-villagers thing might have interested me, if only I had not already read about a quite similar character before, showing an even higher intentness to help others, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2777718.Je_savais_que_je_te_rencontrerais__La_Rose__carlate__1_" title="Je savais que je te rencontrerais (La Rose Écarlate #1) by Patricia Lyfoung" rel="nofollow noopener">Je savais que je te rencontrerais</a> (more than recommended). It might have. But then again, I absolutely and even bizarrely, found <strong>no character</strong> to be exciting.<br /><br />The pacing was okay – not too fast, not too slow. Sometimes, though, events occurred way too rapidly (not letting time to build some substantial emotion inside us) and not enough world-building backed them. I can’t see how this series could get any better if the world-building isn’t upraised to a less simplistic and shallow level.<br /><br /><strong>In short: not recommended.</strong></span>
  <a data-text-id="14056837724402262886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1054900373" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1054900373" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1054900373?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1054900373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5419451636801503932"><b>How many YA fantasy novels have you read?</b><br/><br/>Because I think your enjoyment of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18081228.The_Orphan_Queen__The_Orphan_Queen___1_' title='The Orphan Queen (The Orphan Queen, #1) by Jodi Meadows' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Orphan Queen</a> depends on your answer. This book is not terrible, it is just completely unremarkable. It contains familiar elements that you may recognize from other YA fantasy-lite series - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_' title='Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Throne of Glass</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_' title='Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadow and Bone</a> and the more recent <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17878931.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_' title='Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Red Queen</a>, to name but a few.<br/><br/>Our protagonist is Wilhelmina, the former heir to the throne of her homeland. However, her kingdom was conquered and now she is an Osprey - a kind of </span>
  <span id="freeText5419451636801503932" style="display:none"><b>How many YA fantasy novels have you read?</b><br /><br />Because I think your enjoyment of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18081228.The_Orphan_Queen__The_Orphan_Queen___1_" title="The Orphan Queen (The Orphan Queen, #1) by Jodi Meadows" rel="nofollow noopener">The Orphan Queen</a> depends on your answer. This book is not terrible, it is just completely unremarkable. It contains familiar elements that you may recognize from other YA fantasy-lite series - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_" title="Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a> and the more recent <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17878931.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a>, to name but a few.<br /><br />Our protagonist is Wilhelmina, the former heir to the throne of her homeland. However, her kingdom was conquered and now she is an Osprey - a kind of street gang of thieves. Assuming the identity of nobles from a wraith-fallen kingdom, her and Melanie infiltrate the Skyvale palace.<br /><br />Okay, so first we have the good old <b>ban on magic</b> - a favourite of fantasy authors. Then we have <b>royal politics</b> and a throne at the centre of a dispute about who belongs on it. Then we have the heroine <b>pretending to be someone else</b> whilst socializing with the royal enemy - which I'm sure, if I remember correctly, happens in some form in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_" title="Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17878931.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a>.<br /><br />Plus, the whole infiltration of the palace seems very ill-planned. I got the sense that Wilhelmina and Melanie didn't have a damn clue what they were doing. They turned up, <b>put on pretty gowns, danced at a ball, disliked bitchy women with better curves and flirted with soldiers</b>. If any useful information about the kingdom happened to fall in their laps while they were busy twirling around and drinking wine, then it wasn't because of anything clever or sneaky that they did.<br /><br />The most exciting and unique things about this novel are the least explored. One being the Ospreys, and the other being the masked vigilante called The Black Knife. Neither get much page time. And I suppose I should mention at some point that there is almost <b>zero world-building</b>. The closest thing we get to that is when Connor and Ezra recite the history of magic and the kingdoms in chapter one; it feels like a very awkward way to try and slip in some world background.<br /><br />I am thankful for the lack of romance, but the plot just feels so recycled and Wilhelmina never inspired any kind of emotion in me. Also, this is just speculation so take it with a pinch of salt, but I definitely see potential for a future love triangle brewing in here. <br /><br /><b>Recommended for YA fantasy newcomers or those who genuinely do enjoy reading similar things again and again.</b><br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5419451636801503932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1276662708" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1276662708" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1276662708?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22544152-the-orphan-queen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=cover-whore">cover-whore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=cliffhanger-boo-hiss">cliffhanger-boo-hiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1276662708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2356263654946744254"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2016/01/the-orphan-queen-by-jodi-meadows-jessicadhaluska.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>There are a lot of things wrong with this book. A <i>lot</i>, a lot. Probably more than five. I'll make a list later, but I want it to be clear that ORPHAN QUEEN is a seriously flawed example of YA fantasy . . . Before I tell you that I kind of liked it anyway.<br/><br/>*shrugs awkwardly*<br/><br/>THE HEART WANTS WHAT THE HEART WANTS.<br/><br/><b>Issues:</b><br/><br/><b>1. Plot twists not so twisty.</b> And WORSE, Wil (short for Wilhelmina which is a-whole-nother problem) was shocked by them when they played out. <br/><br/>If it had been a s</span>
  <span id="freeText2356263654946744254" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2016/01/the-orphan-queen-by-jodi-meadows-jessicadhaluska.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>There are a lot of things wrong with this book. A <i>lot</i>, a lot. Probably more than five. I'll make a list later, but I want it to be clear that ORPHAN QUEEN is a seriously flawed example of YA fantasy . . . Before I tell you that I kind of liked it anyway.<br><br>*shrugs awkwardly*<br><br>THE HEART WANTS WHAT THE HEART WANTS.<br><br><b>Issues:</b><br><br><b>1. Plot twists not so twisty.</b> And WORSE, Wil (short for Wilhelmina which is a-whole-nother problem) was shocked by them when they played out. <br><br>If it had been a singular instance, like when the identity of Black Knife (a vigilante . . . named Black Knife . . .) was revealed, I probably would've let it go. <br><br>But it wasn't.<br><br><b>2. Bad lingo.</b> This is a problem with <i>layers</i>.<br><br>Why do you need new colloquialisms in a YA fantasy duology? YOU DON'T. <br><br>But. If you're going to do it anyway, it had better be worth the effort, and substituting your pinky finger for your middle finger as a rude gesture does not qualify as worth the effort:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>It took all my self-restraint not to flip my little finger at her.</i>
</blockquote><br>Neither does <i>"say it again"</i> in place of . . ."You can say <i>that </i>again."<br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445808667i/16704626.jpg" width="236" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br><b>3. Wacky shit.</b> Like calling your gang "Ospreys."<br><br>I'll admit they're a bit more fierce in appearance than I expected, but still . . . in a world where other house symbols are dragons and unicorns (&lt;------problems as far as the eye can see), where does a bird commonly confused with water fowl fit in?<br><br>And why the hell would you name a noble line "House of the Unicorn," if it's not in a story for a five-year-old?<br><br>Then there was the time Patrick did <i>the thing </i>I'd been waiting for him to do at a completely baffling moment: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[reveals his intention to be Wil's King--for the good of the kingdom, <i>of course</i>--by flatly stating that if she was "wise," she <i>would</i> marry him. <br><br>And he did this just after she found out the mission she'd been against (but he organized anyway) led to death of two of their members. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>What <i>is</i> that?<br><br><b>4. Poor execution/lack of subtlety.</b> There were multitudes of cool plot-twists-that-could-have-been that were either ruined by Meadows' impatience or by saying things that were obviously happening could <i>not</i> be happening b/c reasons. <br><br>This is also the reason the plot twists weren't so twisty. <br><br><b>6. Grab bag sans any kind of originality.</b> I know there's no such thing as a new idea, but you have to put your own mark on it. You can't just cobble together a bunch of odds and ends, slap a title on it, and call it a day. <br><br><b>7. Ignored obvious solutions</b> and ignoring <i>this </i>obvious solution in particular was ground zero for basically ALL the problems in the last half of the book: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rival King to Wil (who doesn't know she's Wil) about his (the King's) and her parents intentions for her and Tobiah:<br><br><blockquote><i>“We always said that our children would marry and unite the two kingdoms . . ."</i></blockquote>
<br>Wil a couple hundred pages later:<br><br><blockquote>
<i>"Soon, regardless of our actions tonight, our kingdoms would be at war. After all, he couldn’t just </i>give up <i>Aecor to me. Could he? <br>But why would he? Kissing wasn’t a good enough reason, and <b>I couldn’t think of any political advantages to releasing a valuable piece of land, even if it was to stop a minor war."</b></i>
</blockquote>
<br>Really? B/c King already told you what would FIX IT. *headdesk*  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>8. REALLY flimsy main concept.</b> Use of magic has been outlawed in Wil's world b/c overuse is being blamed for the explosion of BAD magic (called Wraith) into existence, warping and/or destroying anything it comes into contact with. It's covering the land like waves creeping up a beach at high tide. <br><br>But this is all we get:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“That’s the theory,” Clint said. “The overuse of magic triggered a cataclysmic reaction we haven’t been able to reverse.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Except there's very little evidence to support the theory, and what they do have is circumstantial. <br><br>Maybe that's the point, b/c despite Wil's back and forth on the issue, I'm not convinced they haven't been digging their grave with their assumptions. <br><br>BUT if that's the case, the world leaders made BIG decisions based on . . . nothing of substance.<br><br>Either way, it's a problem.<br><br>So yeah . . . a lot of issues. THE ORPHAN QUEEN is definitely not for readers who need well-planned, well-executed, logical worlds and plots. BUT. It was an entertaining and easy read, and when I finished, I didn't want to hunt down Meadows and demand my day back (&lt;------always a good thing). I'd recommend it to someone looking for a brainless way to spend a Saturday. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Pre-review:</b><br><br>B/c I'm in the mood for YA fantasy and who the hell cares that I DNF-ed the first book in Meadows' other series, or that this one apparently ends in an epic cliffhanger of DOOM? <br><br>NOT THIS GIRL.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445866318ra/16712283.gif" width="500" height="343" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>RTC.</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2356263654946744254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1139553548" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1139553548" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1139553548?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1139553548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3054032793368251059">aHHHHHHH OKAY. <b>CLIFFHANGER GOT ME.</b> The first 60% had me, well, <i>intrigued</i> but not won over. Then the ending???? The cliffhanger??? THE CHARACTERS???? MY FEELS??????? (Okay, but my feels are entirely fractured, THANKS FOR NOTHING, BOOK.)<br/><br/>FYI: Make sure you have <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22909838.The_Mirror_King__The_Orphan_Queen___2_' title='The Mirror King (The Orphan Queen, #2) by Jodi Meadows' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Mirror King</a> on hand to read immediately. YOU'LL THANK ME, I SWEAR.)<br/><br/>I'm a gargantuan rabid fantasy fan. I would eat it by the bucket load, probably. <b>While The Orphan Queen wasn't the best TOLD story; it had a ton of awesomely unique eleme</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3054032793368251059" style="display:none">aHHHHHHH OKAY. <b>CLIFFHANGER GOT ME.</b> The first 60% had me, well, <i>intrigued</i> but not won over. Then the ending???? The cliffhanger??? THE CHARACTERS???? MY FEELS??????? (Okay, but my feels are entirely fractured, THANKS FOR NOTHING, BOOK.)<br /><br />FYI: Make sure you have <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22909838.The_Mirror_King__The_Orphan_Queen___2_" title="The Mirror King (The Orphan Queen, #2) by Jodi Meadows" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mirror King</a> on hand to read immediately. YOU'LL THANK ME, I SWEAR.)<br /><br />I'm a gargantuan rabid fantasy fan. I would eat it by the bucket load, probably. <b>While The Orphan Queen wasn't the best TOLD story; it had a ton of awesomely unique elements.</b> Aka -- BATMAN. Ahem. Okay, totally not batman. <i>But</i> it had a Batman like epic-fantasy-medieval-ish character and 'scuse me but I'M IN LOVE WITH THAT IDEA. Plus it was NEW. Ahhhhhhhh!!!!<br /><br />And it also had <b>destroyed kingdoms, and lost princesses, and spies and the occasional murder.</b> What is not to love here?<br /><br /><b>Although, tbh, the plot was kind of slow.</b><br />Like I said, that first 60%? Eh, eh. It felt <i>average</i>? It reminded me a lot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles___1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a> (WHICH I ADORE BTW). And while it had a TON of cool stuff (aka hidden identities and evil magic and stabby things) I just wasn't impressed? Plus the badass and awesome princess spent a LOT of time masquerading as a clueless Duchess and attending balls etc etc. Merp. I preferred when she was out and about being AWESOME.<br /><br /><b>And the protagonist? Wil?</b><br />I mean, I LIKED HER. She didn't seem particularly different to Every Other Hidden Princess Ever. BUT I STILL LIKE THAT TROPE SO ALL IS GOOD. And <b>Omg her slow burning attraction/romance to the viglante, Black Knife, was basically my favourite thing.</b> And ALSO! Will had an epic female BFF, which (shamefully) doesn't happen enough in books. I LIKE.<br /><br /><b>ALSO MAGIC STUFF.</b><br />Magic is illegal, because fun stuff alway is, dangit. But Wil ANIMATES THINGS. She says "wake up" to the wall and it eats a person. LIKE WHY CAN'T I HAVE THIS ABILITY????? I would totally have the kitchen cooking for me and life would be <i>perfect</i>. Ahem. I digress. <b>I though this was an unusual an interesting magical twist!</b><br /><br />(Although I don't get what the "wraith" actually is? It's evil and magic...and the kingdoms banned magic because of wraith. BUT WHAT IS WRAITH EXACTLY????? Like the negative impact of magic? Idek. I'm confused.)<br /><br /><b>World building = very very good.</b><br />It actually felt like a fully complex and rounded world. HUZZAH! FOR ONCE!!<br /><br /><b>DID I MENTION THE FREAKING AWESOME HORRIBLE CLIFFHANGER?????</b><br />That puddle of feels on the floor slowly crying and shaking IS ME by the way.<br /><br />....okay but I do have <b>a few negatives:</b><br />• Obviously the fact that the beginning wasn't great.<br />• Then that Wil wasn't altogether remarkable.<br />• I TOTALLY KNEW WHO BLACK KNIFE WAS THE MOMENT HE WAS INTRODUCED. Am I a genius or was it far too obvious??<br />• Black Knife was <i>not</i> Batman, and this makes me sad though.<br />• There was literally like, one, mention of food. *sad noises*<br />• Where was the cake?<br />• The secondary characters were all rather GALOOMPH and without interesting, individual personalities.<br />• Tons of info dumping.<br /><br /><br /><b>Least to say: I'M A FAN.</b> This is also my first Jodi Meadows books aND NOW I WANT TO READ EVERYTHING BY HER. EEEEEP. I absolutely <i>adored</i> the last 30% especially with the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[reveal of Black Knife being the prince -- CALLED IT -- and the wraith evil magic turning into a creepy boy -- OMG I CANNOT WAIT FOR MORE OF THIS <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. And I'm invested! I want to see Wil getting her throne back. And like the world. And I like the cover (#important). And dangit I WANT THE SEQUEL YESTERDAY.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3054032793368251059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Up the godddamn wazoo <br><br><b>In all honesty I really adored this book.</b> We have a snooty prince, a group of thieves, a city vigilante, a toxic mist, and a total badasss named Willa <br><br><b>Willa</b> is what really made this whole book reach another level. I was really looking for something MORE than the basic --"hi there, imma baddie who hits stuff really hard"-- vibes that the past couple books hEaViLy relied upon to describe their heroine. <br><br>But then there's our heroine, Wilhelmina, who has a hundred identities. She is a princess. She is a spy. <b>She is a threat.</b> And now one of my favorite heroines !! <br><br>And what has she been up to?? Oh you know just <b>leading a group of thieves</b> that look out for each other and rob shitty people. But its totally for a great cause .... of taking over a kingdom !!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507998771ra/24173590.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>

At first <b>Willa</b> recognized <b>Tobias</b> as prince and he only knew her as thief. <br><br>But there is so much more to these characters! <br><br>They each have histories and motivations and goals...<b>and they both lowkey assholes</b> I mean people willing to do whatever it makes to get their way <i>* yah I ship it*</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522179456ra/25281946.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The way the author built up each of these characters, <b> each working their own manipulations <u>while toxic magic is spreading across the land</u> and gangs and rebellions and GODITWASSOFUCKINGGOOD!!!!</b> <br><br>The only thing that kept this book from a 5 star for me was a cliche <b>thats even worse than a love triangle</b><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The prince was black knife. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> like come on, this honestly made me so sad because it just made the whole book lose an element to me.<br><br>Really, without the whole royalty shit I would love to just read a book about <b>Black Knife, kingdom vigilante and Nameless girl strong leader of her gang</b>. <div id="review_643822718" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/643822718" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/643822718?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2015-releases">2015-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer643822718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5790871255321460104">Dang. I've had this book added on my TBR list since June 17, 2013. WOW.<br/><br/><br/><br/>Anyway. HOLY GUACAMOLE. 4.5 stars? The ending makes the rating take a hit, because I hate cliffhanger-like endings. BUT OMG HOW CAN I POSSIBLY WAIT UNTIL 2016 FOR BOOK TWO?! :O<br/><br/><br/><br/>***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/02/review-orphan-queen-by-jodi-meadows.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>The Orphan Queen by Jodi Meadows<br/>Book One of The Orphan Queen series<br/>Publisher: Katherine Tegen Books<br/>Publication Date: March 10, 2015<br/>Rating: 4 stars<br/>Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br/><br/>Summary (from Goodreads):<br/><br/>Wi</span>
  <span id="freeText5790871255321460104" style="display:none">Dang. I've had this book added on my TBR list since June 17, 2013. WOW.<br /><br /><br /><br />Anyway. HOLY GUACAMOLE. 4.5 stars? The ending makes the rating take a hit, because I hate cliffhanger-like endings. BUT OMG HOW CAN I POSSIBLY WAIT UNTIL 2016 FOR BOOK TWO?! :O<br /><br /><br /><br />***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/02/review-orphan-queen-by-jodi-meadows.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />The Orphan Queen by Jodi Meadows<br />Book One of The Orphan Queen series<br />Publisher: Katherine Tegen Books<br />Publication Date: March 10, 2015<br />Rating: 4 stars<br />Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />Wilhelmina has a hundred identities.<br /><br />She is a princess. When the Indigo Kingdom conquered her homeland, Wilhelmina and other orphaned children of nobility were taken to Skyvale, the Indigo Kingdom’s capital. Ten years later, they are the Ospreys, experts at stealth and theft. With them, Wilhelmina means to take back her throne.<br /><br />She is a spy. Wil and her best friend, Melanie, infiltrate Skyvale Palace to study their foes. They assume the identities of nobles from a wraith-fallen kingdom, but enemies fill the palace, and Melanie’s behavior grows suspicious. With Osprey missions becoming increasingly dangerous and their leader more unstable, Wil can’t trust anyone.<br /><br />She is a threat. Wraith is the toxic by-product of magic, and for a century using magic has been forbidden. Still the wraith pours across the continent, reshaping the land and animals into fresh horrors. Soon it will reach the Indigo Kingdom. Wilhelmina’s magic might be the key to stopping the wraith, but if the vigilante Black Knife discovers Wil’s magic, she will vanish like all the others<br /><br />Jodi Meadows introduces a vivid new fantasy full of intrigue, romance, dangerous magic, and one girl’s battle to reclaim her place in the world.<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />Holy guacamole. This book. The ending. Oh my gosh. I literally just finished the book, so bear with me as I write this review. So... my review might not be thoroughly coherent. It might just be a bunch of flails. I might not even make it through the entire review. OH GOSH MY HEART.<br /><br />Wil is an orphan, a princess - orphan queen - of Aecor. She and a ragtag group of orphans from Aecor are trying to take back Aecor. To do so, she and her friend Melanie masquerade as destitute nobles of Liadia, so that they can have refuge in the Skyvale Palace... and get information about Aecor, the armies of the Indigo Kingdom, anything useful that could aid the Ospreys (Wil and her group) in their attempt to reclaim Aecor. But little go as planned with the presence of wraith, Black Knife, and a danger against which even Wil cannot guard herself.<br /><br />I love fantasy. I love epic fantasy. I love high fantasy. Basically, I love fantasy (if you couldn't already tell). It's my favorite genre, and I can't ever seem to get enough. I especially love fantasy in YA literature, because it's amazing and creative and wonderful, but not heavy and boring (like in adult fiction - in my opinion). Jodi Meadows masterfully creates the world in this book. Her writing is lush and rich, and her world-building is very thorough and imaginative. I had no problems picturing the towns, palace, and other locations in my mind. <br /><br />Wil is a very likable heroine. It was easy to root for her throughout the book, it was easy to see her side of things, it was easy to like her. She is brave and fierce, selfless and intelligent. I liked the way her mind works, the way she thought through things. She stood toe-to-toe with Patrick (the Aecor boy who saved her and other Aecor orphans), challenging his ruthless decisions. She never threw her title in any of the Ospreys' faces, but she always commanded authority when she felt necessary. She fought with Black Knife (the vigilante who has actually been killing wraith creatures, which is pretty noble). She pretended to be a dead noble for weeks, and did an excellent job of it. I really liked Wil, and I hope I continue liking her in this series!<br /><br />There are so many amazing secondary characters in this novel! Wil's best friend, Melanie, accompanies her to the palace, also a dead noble. I liked Melanie, though I definitely questioned her loyalty and her being at times. There was Black Knife, a masked vigilante who is curious about Wil, and always seems to find her. There is James, the prince's cousin and guard, who is a great friend to Wil. He's hilarious, and very flirtatious and sweet. There is the prince himself, who is (as Wil says) "sour". I liked him though. The Ospreys - the orphans from Aecor who are helping Wil reclaim her kingdom. So many well-written, three-dimensional characters that I loved. <br /><br />This book is broken up into three parts. Wil goes to the palace with Melanie, to obtain necessary information for their plans. But there are things that Wil is curious about, like wraith in Liadia. Wil goes to investigate the fallen Liadian barrier, hoping that no one at the palace will question her feigned illness. I love that there is more than one plot in this book, more than one story. Wil needs to sneak around the palace, to get information. Wil is trying to find out more about wraith and the wraithlands. Wil is also leaving the palace at night, and sometimes tangles with Black Knife (meaning they fight and threaten each other, and possibly kill wraith creatures every now and then). There is a lot going on in this book, so you can't get bored... you might get bored with one part of the story (probably not though), and there is another part of the story to pick you up!<br /><br />There IS romance in this book. I'm purposefully not saying much about the specifics, who is who. But I will say that I LOVE the romance. It's complicated, it's twisted, it's difficult - and what's new, when it comes to romance in fantasy novels? But there isn't a love triangle, there is no insta-love, and I have high hopes for the romance (though I probably should be more wary, for certain specific reasons).<br /><br />The ending is AWFUL. Awful as in awfully heartbreaking. I hate the ending, but it definitely adds to the story, and I see why the author chose to end this book in such a way. It's cliffhanger-y, so if you hate those, perhaps you might be better off waiting until closer to book two's publication (in 2016?!). But then, we'll probably have to wait for a book three... reading and waiting for books is so difficult! ****EDIT: the author confirmed that there will only be two books in this series - a duology! So, not too much waiting.<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />This book loses an entire star from me because of the ending. The cliffhanger is so mean. Like I said above, I get it, but... it's a heartbreaking ending. And so this book gets one less star. Sorry not sorry.<br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />I TOTALLY RECOMMEND THIS BOOK TO EVERYONE! Fantasy lovers especially, but anyone who enjoys a well-written story (so like, all readers?). Just beware of the ending - it WILL break you. You might be better off waiting for a completed series (see my edit above though - there are only two books to this series!). But hey, I'm not trying to make anyone's decisions for them. I obviously couldn't wait to read this one, so, I'll just suffer quietly.<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />4.5 stars -&gt; rounded down to 4 stars. Because of that ending. I love/hate it. I love this book though. It's definitely a favorite so far (despite not earning a 5-star rating), and I can't wait to read the novellas, and the sequel novel! In 2016. Ugh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5790871255321460104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1132374123?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1132374123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9779888118659106882">Guess who stayed up all night reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18081228.The_Orphan_Queen__The_Orphan_Queen___1_' title='The Orphan Queen (The Orphan Queen, #1) by Jodi Meadows' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Orphan Queen</a> and now looks like a mutant zombie that feeds on coffee!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461510393ra/18875826.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I was Julianna,a general,and occassionally the orphaned Princess of Aecor.I was anyone I needed to be.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Being the heir of a conquered kingdom,Wilhelmina will do anything to free her people and avenge her family.She knows how to fight,to steal,to forge,to spy and now she has to accomplish the most dangerous task of all;impersonate a duchess and gather intelligence on her enem</span>
  <span id="freeText9779888118659106882" style="display:none">Guess who stayed up all night reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18081228.The_Orphan_Queen__The_Orphan_Queen___1_" title="The Orphan Queen (The Orphan Queen, #1) by Jodi Meadows" rel="nofollow noopener">The Orphan Queen</a> and now looks like a mutant zombie that feeds on coffee!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461510393ra/18875826.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I was Julianna,a general,and occassionally the orphaned Princess of Aecor.I was anyone I needed to be.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Being the heir of a conquered kingdom,Wilhelmina will do anything to free her people and avenge her family.She knows how to fight,to steal,to forge,to spy and now she has to accomplish the most dangerous task of all;impersonate a duchess and gather intelligence on her enemy's whereabouts.Without her loyal friends by her side,she must choose carefully who to trust and find a way to defeat the tainted magic that threatens to destroy and alter any form of life.But what if her beliefs are shaken and the enemy is not the monster she thought he is?What if the vigilante known as the Black Knife is right and people who wield magic must be stopped in order to save the world?What if her heart betrayes her and beats for the wrong man?<b>Between balls and fights,deception and stolen kisses,in a city full of mirrors,Wilhelmina will find out what is the cost of taking her kingdom back and whether she can afford to pay the price.</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“People will come to our call when they hear we have the most important piece of all:Princess Wilhelmina.She's alive.She's with us.And she's going to take back her kingdom.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I'd wanted to read this book for a while,but the mixed reviews made me hesitate.The thing is,I understand both the positive and the negative ones.I have to admit that it was <b>predictable</b> and many times I wanted to scold the heroes for not seeing the obvious,and some parts <b>lacked originality</b>,especially since I got many <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17399160.Snow_Like_Ashes__Snow_Like_Ashes___1_" title="Snow Like Ashes (Snow Like Ashes, #1) by Sara Raasch" rel="nofollow noopener">Snow Like Ashes</a> vibes with the lost queen and the enslaved people and the miasma.Moreover,the pace was not consistent,there were times I almost lost interest and times I couldn't put it down.<br>Of course you may wonder why I gave it 4 stars then.The answer is simple:<b>despite its flaws,I enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18081228.The_Orphan_Queen__The_Orphan_Queen___1_" title="The Orphan Queen (The Orphan Queen, #1) by Jodi Meadows" rel="nofollow noopener">The Orphan Queen</a> so,so much!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398162782ra/9378334.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>I got everything I wanted,needed and expected!<b>Politics.Intrigue.Balls.Fights against outlaws and monsters.Secret missions.Espionage.An independent and determined heroine.Sweet romance.Forbidden magic.</b>And my personal favorite,<b>a hot vigilante dressed in black!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461512720ra/18876158.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>There were a couple of times when Wil annoyed me,but in general she was a likable heroine,stubborn and fierce,and her need to protect her people was touching!I admired her for having the strength to admit that her parents might have been wrong,and for the way she handled things when she found out Black Knife's commitments,that was very mature of her!The romance wasn't on the spotlight but it developed naturally and managed to give me all the feels,especially towards the end!Speaking of which,I am very glad I decided to wait until <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22909838.The_Mirror_King__The_Orphan_Queen___2_" title="The Mirror King (The Orphan Queen, #2) by Jodi Meadows" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mirror King</a> was published because apparently <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4116488.Jodi_Meadows" title="Jodi Meadows" rel="nofollow noopener">Jodi Meadows</a> is one of <i>those</i> authors.The ones who write cliffhangers from Hell and watch the world burn from their villain lair,rubbing their hands.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461513599ra/18876226.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I was going to have to face the man who'd destroyed my kingdom, and the boy who was the reason.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Do I recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18081228.The_Orphan_Queen__The_Orphan_Queen___1_" title="The Orphan Queen (The Orphan Queen, #1) by Jodi Meadows" rel="nofollow noopener">The Orphan Queen</a>?That depends on your expectations and standards,but personally, I had a great time reading it!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9779888118659106882" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1591998716" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1591998716" />
    <a title="Jenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14772037-jenna"><img alt="Jenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544410363p2/14772037.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1591998716?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna" href="/user/show/14772037-jenna">Jenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">young fantasy lovers (older or more high fantasy lovers may not like it due to it's flaws)</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=fall-2016-tbr">fall-2016-tbr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=4-star-books">4-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772037-jenna?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1591998716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2483425263896579824"><b> For a book with so many mixed reviews, I really liked it!! </b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401352722ra/9791109.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>Wil' short for Wilhelmina is a Princess of a kingdom conquered by the Indigo Kingdom. Orphaned, she and the other children of deceased nobles have banded together. They have spent the last 10 years training, stealing and surviving in the Indigo Kingdom. They are planning to take her kingdom back. <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479010375i/21138810.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Although Wil' has a secret of her own. Magic has been outlawed because of an overwhelming magical mist that is taking over the world called '</span>
  <span id="freeText2483425263896579824" style="display:none"><b> For a book with so many mixed reviews, I really liked it!! </b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401352722ra/9791109.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Wil' short for Wilhelmina is a Princess of a kingdom conquered by the Indigo Kingdom. Orphaned, she and the other children of deceased nobles have banded together. They have spent the last 10 years training, stealing and surviving in the Indigo Kingdom. They are planning to take her kingdom back. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479010375i/21138810.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Although Wil' has a secret of her own. Magic has been outlawed because of an overwhelming magical mist that is taking over the world called 'wraith'. It is believed that magic is the cause of the 'wraith' which is why it was banned. Wil has magic and only uses it in emergencies. Her fellow orphans are unaware because it would make her even more vulnerable. <br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479010375ra/21138811.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The wraith is moving faster and recently destroyed an entire kingdom. With refugees flooding in, Wil's group of orphans (they call themselves the Osprey's) have decided this is the best time to infiltrate the Indigo Kingdom's court. Wil' has to infiltrate her enemy's kingdom while trying to get information for her own uses. This is until she realizes that the wraith is a much more impending issue and she must try to figure out where her priorities will be.<br><br><b> My Review </b><br>This book had some really interesting aspects to it. I really like the idea of the wraith and think it's intriguing and unique. Although one of this books biggest faults, is its predictability. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479062952ra/21144015.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>From the beginning it was easy to predict who would like who, the identities of others and where some loyalties lie. I will say that there were some things I was caught off-guard by which helped me liking this book. Such as <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ making the wraith solid  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br>This book was full of common YA tropes as well.<br>I enjoyed most of the characters, but also feel like Jodi Meadows could go deeper, expand the characters depth, I think that would make for a better series. Like Meredith, I don't want her to be some 2-dimensional character, I want to see depth. I don't even know what is going on with Melanie because although I understand what/why she does stuff, it feels inconsistent to her character. I really like Wilhelmina but she could also use some depth. OVERALL MORE DEPTH OF CHARACTERS PLEASE.<br><br>I believe the first chapter of this book is written as if this were a tv show. <br><b>Sidenote: This series would make an amazing tv show, I have some fab ideas so Jodi Meadows, hit me up! </b><br>One of the first thing I noticed was that the world building strategy was sort of weak for a book. For a TV show, it would work splendidly but as a novel, it could have been incorporated in different ways. <br>The second thing I noticed was the annoying catch phrase Wil and Melanie say CONSTANTLY. 'Say it again'. It is this world's version of 'You can say that again'. My issue is how often they say it. In Harry Potter you don't see Ron saying 'Bloody hell' every single chapter do you?? It is said so often that it actually irritated me. Repeating it a few times in the book would have been fine, but this was too much.<br><br>At first I didn't like the relationship between Wil and Black Knife but I really grew to like it. This series is hard to ship because even though I like Wil and Black Knife together, I don't think I'm at the level of shipping it. They are the characters with the most depth, yet I still find it hard to connect to them.<br><br>This is probably seeming like a really bad review and y'all are probably wondering why I gave it 4/5 stars. WELL I almost gave it 3.5 because there were some serious room for development in this series like I listed above. In contrast, I really enjoyed it. It was a very quick read for me and I just couldn't put it down, I needed to know what happened next. I would not give it above 4 stars due to all the issues, but I can't deny that I enjoyed this book way more than a 3 star book. That is why it earned 4 stars. If the other issues were not there, it probably would have been 5 stars for me. Unfortunately, they are there and I cannot ignore them. I hope in the next book, the mirror king, Jodi Meadows improves.<br><br>Seriously though, I have some AMAZING ideas if this was a tv show. I am super into scriptwriting, editing and filming because I used to want to be a director/producer. So Jodi Meadows, trust me when I say, that if this ever becomes an adaptation, you want me on your team to do this book justice, but to also expand the story with more depth and story arcs needed for a tv show. That's my pitch haha</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2483425263896579824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1344830253" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1344830253" />
    <a title="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader"><img alt="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579173421p2/43850323.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1344830253?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★" href="/user/show/43850323-reynita-maharani-the-night-reader">Reynita Maharani ★ The Night Reader ★</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22544152-the-orphan-queen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

  <b>3.5 Stars</b>
</s> Rounded down to 3 Stars<br><br>Almost ten years ago, an 8 years old prince of Indigo Kingdom was kidnapped and being held hostage at Aecor. The father of the prince was angry. He commanded his armies to rescue her son and killed the king and queen of Aecor. the chaos made Aecor burning in flame. Every adult living in the palace was slaughtered but the king gave mercy to the highborn children and the king and queen's daughter to be brought to Skyvale, The Capital of Indigo Kingdom. But he never found her or the highborn children that were still alive. <br>Almost ten years later, Aecor is different. The people of Aecor are suffering hunger, opperession and crippling taxes and the sudden disapperances of all know flashers. The people of Aecor don't know that they still have hope because Princess Wilhelmina Korte, The future queen of Aecor is still alive and She will take back Aecor. <br><b>She'll do everything to take back Aecor, even she has to risk her own life</b><br><br><b>My Opinion</b><br>the first time I read this book which was a few months ago, I liked it so much wait... No I didn't like it, I loved it so much I even gave 5 Stars to this book and I cried so much at the ending. But after I passed a few months, I didn't really care about reading the second book but I remembered how I loved this book so I decided to re-read it again before reading The Mirror King. <br>this was my expression when I reached 50% of the book<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463227708ra/19095635.gif" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and this was my expression when I reached 80% of the book <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463228055ra/19095680.gif" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>and this was my expression when I finished this book.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463228299ra/19095779.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>honestly, I was so happy when I finished this book and when I read the ending, I was like " Yeah, Yeah, whatever,<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Just pass out already <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> , this is very boring..."*roll eyes* instead of crying like I did when I read it for the first time. <br><br><b>The Romance</b><br>it's slow burn romance, enemies to lovers and No love triangles for sure. <br>at the first time I read it, I actually thought that the romance was really really sweet<br>I seriously don't know what happened to me that time, how could I think the romance was sweet?!?!<br>because at the second time I read the book I totally didn't think the romance was sweet, but it wasn't bad either. it was...quite good but didn't make me swoon. <br><br><b>You must be wondering Why did I give this book 3.5 Stars if I didn't like it?</b><br>I gave this book 3.5 Stars because the story is original and it's pretty good but I don't really like it, just...pretty good. <br><br><b>will I read the sequel of The Orphan Queen?</b><br>Hell no!! I can't make myself to read the second book, I just can't. Tried finishing The Orphan Queen was such a terrible torture to me but I managed to finish it and I <s>was</s> am kind of proud to myself that I could finish this book because while reading it, I thought several times to DNF it.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463229919ra/19096201.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>But I won't tell you not to read this book because I'm not like that</b>, if you want to read this book, then read it maybe you'll like it and I'd love to read your review about it too.<br>Thank you so much for reading my review, guys!! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413046030ra/11459668.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1011216013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1011216013" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1011216013?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1011216013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4906000244209945756">Fantasy! Magic! A lost Queen and her pals try to reclaim their kingdom! Wraiths! Court's politics! Forbidden Love! Pretty book cover! What can go wrong!?<br/><br/>Well, <i>everything</i>, almost everything.<br/><br/>1.5 stars. I'm breathing fire and brimstone after reading the whole book.<br/><br/><b>(1) The heroine and her friend's plan to reclaim their kingdom is *RUBBISH*, plain and simple</b><br/><br/>If you think the rebels in <i>Red Queen</i> and <i>The Young Elites</i> are bad, just wait till you see what the heroine and her friends had done!<br/><br/>Some 19 orpha</span>
  <span id="freeText4906000244209945756" style="display:none">Fantasy! Magic! A lost Queen and her pals try to reclaim their kingdom! Wraiths! Court's politics! Forbidden Love! Pretty book cover! What can go wrong!?<br /><br />Well, <i>everything</i>, almost everything.<br /><br />1.5 stars. I'm breathing fire and brimstone after reading the whole book.<br /><br /><b>(1) The heroine and her friend's plan to reclaim their kingdom is *RUBBISH*, plain and simple</b><br /><br />If you think the rebels in <i>Red Queen</i> and <i>The Young Elites</i> are bad, just wait till you see what the heroine and her friends had done!<br /><br />Some 19 orphans (the Ospreys) banded together to try reclaiming their lost kingdom from the invading kingdom, among them the supposedly 'lost' princess. How will they take back their kingdom? I don't know! After reading a whole book I still don't know! Supposedly they has been stealing to support themselves, some operations had been ran, supposedly there are some resistance groups, but the details and the goals of those Ospreys have hardly been made clear.<br /><br /><b>(2) The court's politics in this book are on the primary school's level</b><br /><br />The Indigo Kingdom and its royal family doesn't do anything to discover the whereabouts of the lost princess! The princess simply walks into the Indigo's court with no disguise even though she knows the crown prince might recognize her! Examples like these are countless in the book! <br /><br /><b>(3) The heroine did a shit job as a spy and a thief</b><br /><br />For example, guards are going to reach the heroine's rooms but she only hides her important items under the mattress?! I have no idea why the publisher still insists on me to believe she is a 'strong woman'!<br /><br /><b>(4) The supposedly fearsome Black Knife turns out to be so lame</b><br /><br />The fearsome Black Knife who fiercely tracks and catches magic-using outlaws with no mercy suddenly decides he doesn't want to turn the magic-using heroine to the polices! And then........teenage romance happens between those two, when the heroine hasn't even seen the guy's face underneath his mask! Last but not least Black Knife also turns out being this....you know who person later on, and I (along with countless other readers out there) can totally see this coming from miles away!<br /><br /><b>(5) Characters with perfectly modern English names like Patrick, James etc and words like 'police' are used in the story, which is supposed to be Fantasy/magical fantasy</b><br /><br />I know, it's a story supposedly takes place in an 18th century European based fantasy world so it is safe to guess this fantasy world would be somewhat similar with our own world. Yet when those perfectly modern English names mentioned above show up in the book, I still feel the author *isn't even trying* when she creates this supposed fantasy world.<br /><br />*sighs* The setting about the destructive wraiths and magic is nice, but too bad that the rest of the book isn't so nice. Still, I will give this sequel a chance just for the sake of finishing a series.<br /><br />Review for book 2: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1973140605">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></span>
