<div id="review_989014972" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/989014972" />
    <a title="Andreea Pop" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop"><img alt="Andreea Pop" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486663526p2/4858513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/989014972?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreea Pop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreea Pop" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop">Andreea Pop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=bat-shit-crazy">bat-shit-crazy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=royalty">royalty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=amazing-feelings">amazing-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=huge-character-development">huge-character-development</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=badass-heroine">badass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=awesome-romance">awesome-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer989014972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4157184909536124362">This beauty of a book, called <i>The Orphan Queen</i>, stole my heart really easily, despite its numerous flaws. <br/><br/><a href='http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-DlOBRL9d2-A/Vd9X-OUpuqI/AAAAAAAAPVg/sKB0HK-eRmI/s1600/tumblr_m1obhaFXos1rn95k2o1_250.gif' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440700982ra/16012072.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I won't lie, the beginning was far from impressive, because probably this book's biggest flaw was its predictability. I saw plot twists from miles away, but what saved the novel from my putting it down was actually the unraveling of said plot twists. It was entertaining and satisfying and done in a clever manner. <br/><br/>Another aspect that had me cringing was the originality. In terms of charac</span>
  <span id="freeText4157184909536124362" style="display:none">This beauty of a book, called <i>The Orphan Queen</i>, stole my heart really easily, despite its numerous flaws. <br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-DlOBRL9d2-A/Vd9X-OUpuqI/AAAAAAAAPVg/sKB0HK-eRmI/s1600/tumblr_m1obhaFXos1rn95k2o1_250.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440700982ra/16012072.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I won't lie, the beginning was far from impressive, because probably this book's biggest flaw was its predictability. I saw plot twists from miles away, but what saved the novel from my putting it down was actually the unraveling of said plot twists. It was entertaining and satisfying and done in a clever manner. <br><br>Another aspect that had me cringing was the originality. In terms of characters, for the first half or so, Tobiah (the Crown Prince of Indigo Kingdom) and James (his bodyguard) were very much Dorian and Chaol from ToG, only with their personalities reversed. Then there's Wilhelmina, a disguised orphan queen who's after taking back her conquered kingdom, and that again struck me as a deja-vu with the newest books in the ToG series, not to mention the whole dynamic between Wil and Tobiah (I'm a sucker for Dorlaena anyway). <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-I8hkKu8bA9w/Vd9aU2LfQPI/AAAAAAAAPWI/vaUIWyQeCss/s1600/ooohsoclose.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="131" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440701353ra/16012117.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Plotwise, the initial opening of the book reminded me a lot of <i>Snow Like Ashes</i>. In both books we have a very small group of rebels fighting to free their country, but in this case the group is made entirely out of teenager orphans and that detail reduced the plausibility of the story -- let's be honest: there's no way a group of children have survived for ten years on the run and trained and actually managed to gain intelligence and information. But hey, it's fantasy. <br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-2DFfOMl2qIs/Vd9bJt-woaI/AAAAAAAAPWQ/cGNxgfarfCE/s1600/tumblr_mnc1k2n14z1r9hc9jo1_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="180" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440701353ra/16012118.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And still. You can see that I could damn the rating of this book for its multiple faults, but I don't because I really really liked it. I loved the characters, I loved the story, I loved the atmosphere and if that doesn't make a story worthwhile, I don't know what does. <br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-lVu3F7g7SjU/Vd9X9eOZ_jI/AAAAAAAAPVY/9ch5As--Mq4/s1600/21af28ecf03ff60b632bca14ee589261.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440700982i/16012073.jpg" width="240" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>For instance, Wil, although no Celaena Sardothien, is a strong heroine, brave and moral and compassionate. She fights her own battles fiercely and it covers up the fact that sometimes she can be incredibly over emotional, overwhelmed and inexperienced. I admired her wonderful development that ensured we will be seeing more of her queenly demeanor. <br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-jYuWdNrdE0M/Vd9X9aSA8EI/AAAAAAAAPVc/TjWBQH3jwng/s1600/0502fe0af6dd3b75251cef9023a1f1f0.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440700982i/16012074.jpg" width="257" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Black Knife -- oh, may I swoon? He was the perfect blend of danger, sarcasm, dedication and selflessness, with a dash of sexy. I loved everything about him and my heart was really happy about his and Wil's developing friendship. <i>Ahem</i>. <br><br><i>
  <b>“The best mask is a face no one will remember.”<br>“Oh,” he said, and looked at me as though I were a mystery. “I don’t see how anyone could forget your face.”</b>
</i><br><br>A small regret is that I would've liked to get to know James better. Melanie, as Wil's best friend, kind of sucked. Oh, and Patrick, cut the crap and stay put. <br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-lMKLOphSZ_w/Vd9bRse1SAI/AAAAAAAAPWY/BKz-tvi8QYo/s1600/tumblr_inline_mo0w2otvu71qz4rgp.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="161" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440701353ra/16012119.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The story itself involves a lot of magic and how its overuse has terrifying consequences -- the creation of the wraith. No one knows what to do with it or how to stop it since it's basically ruining kingdoms every left and right. The Indigo Kingdom is the next in line for its destruction, but soon Aecor (Wil's kingdom) will meet the same fate, so that makes it Wil's responsibility to deal with the unnatural. This plotline offers a lot of excitement and I honestly can't wait to get to know more about magic in the next book. <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-nsUJyjIg8rI/Vd9Y6V1K3JI/AAAAAAAAPWA/Xl_KGlNxM_g/s1600/6141129b00a4890e404af2d98da854ba.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440700982i/16012075.jpg" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I absolutely loved how romance wasn't the main focus of the book, but still somehow managed to be important. It developed naturally and also added a shade of forbidden excitement to the story. And oh my, the romance itself, although never crossing beyond kissing, was all kinds of wonderful, butterflies-inducing and lovely. There was tension, there was slow burning, there were exquisite feelings and finally -- courtesy of that cruel ending that delivered two sucker-punches one after another -- aching yearning, helplessness and deep regret. Perfect. <br><br><i>
  <b>“Why are you always trying to leave me?”</b>
</i><br><br>It's my first book by Jodi Meadows but I assure you it won't be the last. After all, there's still the sequel, <i>The Mirror King</i>, waiting for me in April (but I have faith Edelweiss and HarperCollins will do their mojo and save me the eternal torture). And I just want to add how happy and grateful I am to see this series is a duology! I honestly thought it was going to be a trilogy, but lucky me I was wrong. We need more duologies anyway. <br><br>Coming back to Meadows' books, I'll be sure to pick up her <i>Incarnate</i> series right away since they drew me in with their prettiness a few years ago and now I don't need any more persuasion to read them. Don't expect an extraordinary writing style; it's nothing special or fancy, but she managed to make her world-building compelling even if it's not the definition of awesomeness and I have to give respect where it's due. <br><br>Thrilling from start to finish, threaded with toe-curling romance and woven with enigmatic magical elements, <i>The Orphan Queen</i> is a new favorite of mine and if you're looking for a captivating fantasy read, then I wholeheartedly suggest picking it up. <br><br><b>ENJOY! &lt;3<br></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4157184909536124362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1225874145" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1225874145" />
    <a title="Mandy K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2990684-mandy-k"><img alt="Mandy K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561995080p2/2990684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1225874145?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandy K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandy K" href="/user/show/2990684-mandy-k">Mandy K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2990684-mandy-k?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2990684-mandy-k?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1225874145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10421990422813176843"><a href='http://ohdangmandy.blogspot.com/2015/03/the-orphan-queen-by-jodi-meadows-review.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Full Review</a><br/><br/>I'm still reeling. I stayed up way way late last night, I'm talking 4 hours later than I usually do, because I couldn't go to bed without finishing this book. Let's just say that by the time I finally went to bed, some people where just waking up for work. Yeah. But, it was worth it. Even though the story and characters and ending infiltrated my dreams. <br/><br/>The story pick up in the middle of a robbery, and the story never stops from there. Chock full of spy missions, vigilantism, betrayal</span>
  <span id="freeText10421990422813176843" style="display:none"><a href="http://ohdangmandy.blogspot.com/2015/03/the-orphan-queen-by-jodi-meadows-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Full Review</a><br /><br />I'm still reeling. I stayed up way way late last night, I'm talking 4 hours later than I usually do, because I couldn't go to bed without finishing this book. Let's just say that by the time I finally went to bed, some people where just waking up for work. Yeah. But, it was worth it. Even though the story and characters and ending infiltrated my dreams. <br /><br />The story pick up in the middle of a robbery, and the story never stops from there. Chock full of spy missions, vigilantism, betrayals, secret identities, and plans to take back a kingdom, this books will suck you in and keep you there until the very last page. <br /><br />Beneath all the action is some awesome world building. Magic has been outlawed since Wraith, the byproduct of magic use, has been creeping across the lands devouring and destroying everything. We get to see Glowmen, people who abused wraith like a drug and are now mutated and less than human, wraith creatures, things like kittens and bugs that the wraith has twisted into scary monsters, and all kinds of crazy other anomalies like floating roads and trees growing upside down. The visuals here are great and I can picture all of the terrors from the wraith so vividly. <br /><br />And let me just take a second to rant about that ending. It's cruel, it's criminal, there should be a big ol' warning on the cover: "major devastating cliff hanger, precede with caution". I'm having a hard time articulating how this cliff hanger left me feeling. It's like I was standing a thousand feet up in the air, overlooking one of those views that just brings a bit of hope, and suddenly this trap door opens up underneath and I'm plummeting down down down. There's even #OQsupportgroup on Twitter. <br /><br />I loved the characters here. Wilhelmina, Melanie, the Ospreys, James, Black Knife, even Prince Tobiah and the King. Meadows did a great job making complex characters, especially making you second guess assumptions you made about characters and creating sympathy for certain characters. And can we just take a second to talk about Black Knife? He was my favorite character in the book. I kind of fell a little in love with him. Dark and mysterious, is he a hero? Is he a menace? What are his intentions? Who is he? Just love. <br /><br />I don't read fantasy books too often, and this book had me asking myself: Why the heck not? I can not wait for 2016 to get here so I can see how this story ends. I have to know. Time to build a time machine so I can read The Mirror King.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10421990422813176843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1113284148" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113284148" />
    <a title="Katerina  Kondrenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36306002-katerina-kondrenko"><img alt="Katerina  Kondrenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590049412p2/36306002.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1113284148?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina  Kondrenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina  Kondrenko" href="/user/show/36306002-katerina-kondrenko">Katerina  Kondrenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=trope-royals">trope-royals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=target-young-adult">target-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=reviewed-by-me-full">reviewed-by-me-full</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=04-out-of-10">04-out-of-10</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=pov-female-only">pov-female-only</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=trope-revenge">trope-revenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=imo-good-idea-bad-execution">imo-good-idea-bad-execution</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=friendship-bromance">friendship-bromance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1113284148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9195257639744180500"><b>
  <blockquote>4 out of 10</blockquote>
</b><br/><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog<br/><a href='http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/08/the-orphan-queen-by-jodi-meadows.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br/><br/><b>Short-Soundtrack:</b><br/><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=A4ePCWZbEYo' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carnival Youth - Never Have Enough</a><br/><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iB_eIW0YaRc' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ian Dolamore - Vigilante</a><br/><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=grxNeqq1Xvw' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Raz Ohara and The Odd Orchestra – Kisses</a><br/><br/><b>Genre</b>: high-fantasy, YA<br/><b>Stuff</b>: the wraith, magic, rebels<br/><b>Fail</b>: predictability and uneven writing<br/><b>WOW</b>: the main concept<br/><b>POV</b>: 1st-person, female<br/><b>Love-Geometry</b>: none<br/><br/><b>Quote-Core</b>: <blockquote>“Ma</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText9195257639744180500" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>4 out of 10</blockquote>
</b><br /><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog<br /><a href="http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/08/the-orphan-queen-by-jodi-meadows.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br /><br /><b>Short-Soundtrack:</b><br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=A4ePCWZbEYo" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Carnival Youth - Never Have Enough</a><br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iB_eIW0YaRc" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Ian Dolamore - Vigilante</a><br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=grxNeqq1Xvw" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Raz Ohara and The Odd Orchestra – Kisses</a><br /><br /><b>Genre</b>: high-fantasy, YA<br /><b>Stuff</b>: the wraith, magic, rebels<br /><b>Fail</b>: predictability and uneven writing<br /><b>WOW</b>: the main concept<br /><b>POV</b>: 1st-person, female<br /><b>Love-Geometry</b>: none<br /><br /><b>Quote-Core</b>: <blockquote>“May I get anything for you?” <i>Information. Lists. My kingdom.</i></blockquote><br /><b>
  <i>The Orphan Queen</i>
</b> is a mess. <b>
  <i>Jodi Meadows</i>
</b> created a very interesting world, gave it a solid problem to deal with, but forgot to develop her heroes and grace the plot with logic instead of I-do-what-I-please-ness. Forced twists aren't twists. And feelings toward MCs can't appear out of the blue.<br /> <br />The <b>main idea</b> is good. Magic causes the <b>wraith</b> - an echo of somebody's power, a twisted substance that comes and covers your city up, mummifying everything and everyone, it changes people and animals, making them bigger, vicious and merciless. Many kingdoms had already fall, but those are still standing decided to sign a treaty: magic is treason, no one's allowed to use it. Only <b>Aecor</b> refused to join the alliance, its rulers believed that pre-dosed magic is blessing and shouldn't be completely forbidden. That's why the <b>Indigo Kingdom</b> took over their land. The King and the Queen were killed along with local noblemen during the One-Night-War. Their children were sent to the orphanage, but soon ran away and started to plan revenge.<br /><br />And that is my first complaint. <b>Kids and revolution?</b> Like really? Mind that we speak not of an army of children but of a few little 'warriors' (~15 persons). Their leader - <b>Patrick</b>, a son of the late Aecor's General - has useful acquaintances and sharp mind, the others steal supplies, our MC - <b>Wilhelmina, </b>who is the rightful heir to the vermilion throne - is a pretty talented forger. Good for them, but I'm still not convinced. Also, they ran about 9 years ago? How, may I ask, 3-old-year kids did that? I see no way for them to survive being homeless in a company of 8-10 year-old children as their 'parents'.<br /><br />Well, what do we have in the present? When the wraith conquers yet another county - <b>Liadia</b>, Wilhelmina and her best-friend <b>Melanie</b> go to the <b>Skyvale</b>'s palace (the heart of the Indigo Kingdom), impersonating two dead noblewomen, to spy around and get some crucial information. They are welcomed ('cause, duh, the treaty's condition) and unrecognized (as if not a single person at the court has been in Liadia or Liadia's ladies did never leave their homes). That's how the story starts.<br /><br /><b>Wilhelmina and Co</b> want their kingdom back, never giving a second thought to the fact that their princess knows nothing about ruling. They also blame the Indigo Kingdom for what they've done with Aecor, missing the point - Aecor used magic, magic attracted the wraith, and the wraith means death without any exceptions. No matter how accurate you were or how many good things you committed with spells and powers, consequences are deadly. Sorry, I can't sympathy with the narrow-minded bunch of pseudo-rebels. <br /><br />We have a prince. His names is <b>Tobiah</b> and he's boring. He has a fiance, she's boring too. And he has a cousin, a cliched puppy whom I did like. <br /><br />We have a masked vigilante, who fights Glowing Men (people corrupted with the wraith), chasing criminals and bringing justice in da Zorro-style. They call him <b>Black Knife</b> (which is a bit ridiculous, but not as much as visible bruises after slaps or flicking of little finger instead of showing a middle one, just imagine this gesture and laugh your ass out) and have no idea who's hiding behind the mask. Ooookay, they haven't, but readers do! And I was really surprised to see in the authors review for the first of Black Knife's novellas that they would be spoiler-ish for the first installment because of the vigilante's identity. Was it supposed to be a secret? <br /><br />Wil hates Tobiah (and her reason is fucking lame), Wil is intrigued with the Black Knife. She meets him on the streets to work together from time to time, and they slowly falling in love. Which is leading us to, <b>the romance</b>, yeah... Meadows is good with romantic scenes (the one with a blindfold, a silk mask and a lot of kisses was really hot), but fails when it comes to creating tension, building love-suspense and doing a proper development of characters interactions. During the kissing scene I was shipping the heroes hard, but before and after had nothing in me to ache for this couple.<br /><br />The <b>writing</b> was bad. Not the wording (which was fine), but the way author reveals her story: it's either naked info-dumping or rushed retelling. The book needed a better editing. Some parts were underdeveloped while some overdone. Potential twists had no chance to shine. Simplicity of relationships and shallow dialogues didn't help either.<br /><br />Someone had to tell <i>Jodi Meadows</i> that her <b>plot</b> was made of contrived coincidences. And <i>that</i>, that unforgivable. Shit has to happen and not only when MC is ready for it. People have to act as real persons and not as marionettes.<br /><br />The <b>ending</b> wasn't shocking, 'cause Meadows gave us too many clues. Why oh why? If you want to torture your readers, do it without preludes. I've been more devastated after way happier finals. Here I knew what would happen and that it would mean nothing, 'cause we'd already seen the same situation in a one of the previous chapters.<br /><br /><b>Now to the WTFs those would contain spoilers.</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[- Chey knew from the start that Wil wasn't her friend from Liadia, so why didn't she tell anyone? She's been in Liadia, she had letters from the real Julianna, everyone would believe her. It's been weeks and she said no word. Weeks!! What a nonsense! If somebody would come to my home, pretending to be my supposedly dead friend, I'll be furious and will not allow this person to have a good time. <br /><br />- What kind of guards does the palace have? Why Wil and her Ospreys could so easily slipping in and out without anyone noticing? And don't remind me of their investigation, they couldn't know shifts of each guard at the palace, plus good guards change their schemes and time-lines quite often. And how could Patrick kill the king? He had to have personal guards at his doors! The window? I don't think one can to enter the king's windows that simple. <br /><br />- What the fuck with not checking the lake? I mean, you have a lot of brave men, send a few to investigate the damned thing which may save all of your asses in the future. Yes, they may die (heroically!). But sitting and chatting and waiting for the wraith to come and kill you all isn't a better choice, is it? You all deserve too die. Wil can stay, 'cause she had balls to go the Wraithland. <br /><br />- When someone mentions in your presence something that resurrects bad memories of your past, what are you doing? Choking? Gasping? Maybe you cannot breath? 'Cause Wil acts just like that. She can be silent for a few minutes like in a trance or almost faints, 'cause that's so unbearable. Why her balls don't help her in suchlike situations? In the end, when Tobiah did say that he'd marry Meredith soon, she thought of what a good pretender she was to give away nothing of her emotions. But when somebody was talking about Aecor, she was always pulling a bad soap-opera's actress on. That's inconsistent. <br /><br />- Tobiah promoted James to a captain and now this new captain would have to oversee all the palace guards. What a stupid decision! The boy has no experience in such a work, also he was Tobiah's bodyguard whom the prince could trust with his life and secrets, but after this promotion he wouldn't be able to do both jobs. <br /><br />- Matches. They have matches. We've got them only in the 19th century! And we never had magic. I'm sure, their scientists couldn't come up with matches that soon after magic became forbidden.<br /><br />- I can't understand how Wil didn't recognize Tobiah in Black Knife. He couldn't change his voice so much, his eyes and eyebrows were always visible, the prince was known as a lover of long sleep... But not a single bell rang in Wil's head. She never suspected him. Never.<br /><br />- The wraith-boy couldn't find Patrick, but when Patrick came to kill the prince he was there too. Seriously? This creepy little thing couldn't do nothing during a week? How convenient for the plot! Just like everything else is.<br /><br />There are more weird details, I guess. But I'm too lazy to bring them all up. I just hope you see what did bother me this much that I gave the book only 4 out of 10 stars. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br /><b>To read or not to read</b> is up to you. This isn't the worst book ever, it has the good moments, but it lacks too many important things to actually blow your mind, especially if you prefer your reads to be well-thought-out, logical and unpredictable.<br /><br /><b>PS</b>: I will continue with this series hoping for more kissing scenes. I can't deny that <b>
  <i>Jodi Meadows</i>
</b> knows how to write them.<br /><br /><b>The Orphan Queen (Королева сирот):</b><br /><blockquote>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113284072" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hidden Prince (Оберегаемый принц)</a> #0.1/2<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113284084" rel="nofollow noopener">The Glowing Knight (Раскаленный рыцарь)</a> #0.2/2<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1730639036" rel="nofollow noopener">The Burning Hand (Пылающая рука)</a> #0.3/2<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113284108" rel="nofollow noopener">The Black Knife (Черный нож)</a> #0.4/2<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113284148" rel="nofollow noopener">The Orphan Queen (Королева сирот)</a> #1/2<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113284161" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mirror King (Зеркальный король)</a> #2/2</blockquote></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11328378804469350094">I did not expect to like this one... but I was actually really pleasantly surprised. I went into it with low expectations based on friends ratings - but I actually rather enjoyed myself reading it. <br/><br/>I thought about landing this around 3-3.5 stars but when I think back.. I was pretty giddy during many scenes and I really enjoyed myself. Definitely had some nice feels.   <span id="freeText11328378804469350094" style="display:none">I did not expect to like this one... but I was actually really pleasantly surprised. I went into it with low expectations based on friends ratings - but I actually rather enjoyed myself reading it. <br /><br />I thought about landing this around 3-3.5 stars but when I think back.. I was pretty giddy during many scenes and I really enjoyed myself. Definitely had some nice feels. This was a mashup between "Ruined" by Amy Tintera and "Snow Like Ashes" by Sara Raasch. <br /><br /><b>For those of you who are interested.. let me help you out with what to expect.</b><br /><br />1. This book is definitely cliche and full of YA tropes (i.e. lost princess) ... but I didn't really care because I know what I like to read. <br />2. It is predictable. Whatever. While I could predict *who* certain people where and such.. I still enjoyed watching the characters figure out the plot twists.<i> Plus... who doesn't love a man in a mask regardless if you know who he is?</i><br />3. The world building was weak and the magic was not explained well at all. I still enjoyed the premise regardless... at least it wasn't a crazy info dump. <br /><br />Either way, even with these complaints aside.. I actually had a lot of fun. I liked the heroine enough (though can someone please tell me how you come up with a name like "Wilhelmina"... I couldn't get past that one.) I actually enjoyed the bit of chemistry between Wil and Black Knife. <br /><br />All that to say- I already got book 2 and I'm gonna go read that now.. yay! <br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/herbookishthings/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>

I would love to see what happens next even though the last 10% of the book were a bit confusing and at times hard to follow. We shall see.</span>

<div id="review_971816591" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/971816591" />
    <a title="Sophie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8563233-sophie"><img alt="Sophie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564510350p2/8563233.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/971816591?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie" href="/user/show/8563233-sophie">Sophie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=2015-releases">2015-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer971816591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12635766404380792603">My god, this book was utter perfection! Ever since ARC reviews began to appear in the blogosphere there has been a ton of hype surrounding this book, hype that was not misplaced. For some reason, I was still hesitant to read it. Perhaps I thought the hype would ruin the reading experience, or something like that. However, this was not the case at all.<br/><br/>In The Orphan Queen, we follow our heroine, Wil, as she tries to infiltrate the main palace of the Indigo Kingdom, whom had conquered her kingdom o</span>
  <span id="freeText12635766404380792603" style="display:none">My god, this book was utter perfection! Ever since ARC reviews began to appear in the blogosphere there has been a ton of hype surrounding this book, hype that was not misplaced. For some reason, I was still hesitant to read it. Perhaps I thought the hype would ruin the reading experience, or something like that. However, this was not the case at all.<br /><br />In The Orphan Queen, we follow our heroine, Wil, as she tries to infiltrate the main palace of the Indigo Kingdom, whom had conquered her kingdom of Aecor nearly ten years earlier. Her motive for the infiltration is simple: to discover vital information which will help her to retake her throne. However, not all is as it seems. For the past 100 years, the Indigo Kingdom had banned the use of magic, as the industrialisation of magic had brought wraith to the land, destroying everything in its wake. Wil's use of magic in emergencies catches causes problems that have major consequences. On top of all of this, she has to deal with her conflicting emotions about Black Knife, the so-called vigilante who, rather than capture her for using magic, enlists her help in ridding the city from the wraith problem. Though he could lead to her ruin, she grows more and more attached to him, an attachment that nothing good can come from, especially when she discovers his identity.<br /><br />Having a wonderful protagonist makes any book special, and this was no exception. Wilhelmina was a spunky, fierce princess, who'd faced major hardship since the assassination of her parents and the loss of her kingdom. Through all of this, she has remained strong, and does everything in her power to reclaim her lost throne. I loved everything about Wil, and kind of wish she was my best friend. She is fiercely loyal her fellow orphans, the Ospreys, and is reclaiming Aecor as much for them as she is for herself. Even when faced with solutions that could make everything easier in the long run, she stands her ground, and sticks by her morals. She goes after what she thinks is right, and isn't shy about stating her disapproval.<br /><br />To make this book even better, if possible, the love interest was someone who helped to make Wil better. Black Knife was mysterious, though I had guessed who he was, but then talked myself out of it. Whereas he knew stuff about Wil that could have hurt her, and her chances of reclaiming Aecor, he never told on her. He went so far as to help her at every possible opportunity, following her as far as he could when she went into the wraith lands. Their relationship was also slow-burning, just the right amount of longing so that it didn't turn into a complete angst-fest. I was extremely glad with how the big reveal occurred, though I'm apprehensive with the amount of angst and suffering will be in book 2, The Mirror King, considering the cliffhanger-y ending.<br /><br />Out of all the characters, the only one I disliked was Patrick, who, to me, was a condescending SoB, who deserved a good slap. He was presumptive, and rash, and even though he said he was loyal to his princess, his queen, his actions were not in her best interests. When more is discovered about his father, the old General, he seemed more and more like him, and his actions could be the ruin of Wil. Hopefully, he'll get his comeuppance in The Mirror King.<br /><br />This book is a wonderful new addition of the high fantasy genre, and lovers of that will adore this book. From The Orphan Queen I have a ton of new fave's: a new favourite heroine, a new favourite world, and a new OTP. The wait to April seems far too long, but luckily there is the #OQsupportgroup to help. Quite frankly, you should just go out, buy this book, and read it ASAP - you will not be disappointed!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12635766404380792603" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8787594180850374848">I had a great time with this book. Strong heroine, magic, monsters, espionage, battle against evil...everything I like about fantasy neatly packaged into one; what’s not to like?<br/>A 17-year-old Wil, heiress to a fallen kingdom, after 10 years of hiding with other kids of nobility, went under disguise, infiltrating the palace with plans to take back her kingdom.<br/>The mission got complicated quickly, first she crossed paths with a vigilante named black knife, and partnered up with him despite her disl</span>
  <span id="freeText8787594180850374848" style="display:none">I had a great time with this book. Strong heroine, magic, monsters, espionage, battle against evil...everything I like about fantasy neatly packaged into one; what’s not to like?<br />A 17-year-old Wil, heiress to a fallen kingdom, after 10 years of hiding with other kids of nobility, went under disguise, infiltrating the palace with plans to take back her kingdom.<br />The mission got complicated quickly, first she crossed paths with a vigilante named black knife, and partnered up with him despite her dislike of him taking the law into his hands, then she started disagreeing with the leader of the refugee group that led the mission. One thing was clear through it all, there are certain moral boundaries she won’t cross.<br />It was a fantastic read, ended with a cliffhanger, heading off to find out what’s next in the second book. 5 stars!</span>

<div id="review_709278738" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/709278738" />
    <a title="Nemo (The Moonlight Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library"><img alt="Nemo (The Moonlight Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560136145p2/11289146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/709278738?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nemo (The Moonlight Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nemo (The Moonlight Library)" href="/user/show/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library">Nemo (The Moonlight Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22544152-the-orphan-queen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=format-ebook">format-ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=genre-high-fantasy">genre-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=2015-published">2015-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=source-edelweiss">source-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=audience-young-adult">audience-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=beautiful-covers">beautiful-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=i-like-princesses">i-like-princesses</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=publisher-5-harpercollins">publisher-5-harpercollins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=series-to-finish">series-to-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer709278738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16681263153355731511"><a href='http://moonlightlibrary.com/2014/12/18/arc-review-orphan-queen-jodi-meadows/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>This review was originally posted on The Moonlight Library</a><p>
  <em>Please note: this is a review of the sample offered on Edelweiss, which was about one-third of the total book (Part 1), and is not a review of the complete book.</em>
  <br/>
</p><p>SUMMARY<br/></p><p>Wilhemenia is the orphaned queen of a conquered kingdom, a girl disguised as a refugee duchess in an enemy kingdom helping to free her enslaved people and their right to use magic even though other kingdoms believe wraith, a dangerous by-product of magic, is slowly d</p></span>
  <span id="freeText16681263153355731511" style="display:none"><a href="http://moonlightlibrary.com/2014/12/18/arc-review-orphan-queen-jodi-meadows/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">This review was originally posted on The Moonlight Library</a><p>
  <em>Please note: this is a review of the sample offered on Edelweiss, which was about one-third of the total book (Part 1), and is not a review of the complete book.</em>
  <br />
</p><p>SUMMARY<br /></p><p>Wilhemenia is the orphaned queen of a conquered kingdom, a girl disguised as a refugee duchess in an enemy kingdom helping to free her enslaved people and their right to use magic even though other kingdoms believe wraith, a dangerous by-product of magic, is slowly destroying the world.<br /></p><p>WORLDBUILDING<br /></p><p>The worldbuilding in this book is phenomenal – there’s so much culture and different beliefs and even small gestures and sayings used by the characters. The one issue I had with it is how much of the world-building is relayed through dialogue – even Wil herself acknowledges that people are reciting lessons or indulging in hearing their own voices. Perhaps I would be more sympathetic if the words were coming from Wil herself – there’s nothing wrong with passing on information and world-building so long as it doesn’t interrupt the flow of the story. I also wish I had access to the map that’s supposed to be in the beginning of this book, because the three main kingdoms and the minor ones around them sound so interesting, and also because the main threat is environmental and moving ever closer, so I’d like a better grasp on how much wraith has eaten how much kingdom.<br /></p><p>CHARACTER<br /></p><p>Wilheminia is pretending to be Duchess Juliana of Liania, which has fallen to wraith. She’s really the lost orphaned queen of Aecor, on the other side of the Indigo Kingdom, which forced other kingdoms into signing a no-magic agreement in an effort to curb the wraith. Wil’s a totally awesome character – she’s quick with her mind, wits, her physicality and her bravery. Oh, and she’s an illegal magic user, and I’m pretty sure none of her gang, the Ospreys, know that. Other characters of note include Melanie, who’s up to something she won’t let Wil in on; Tobiah, the surly crown prince of the Indigo Kingdom, who’s newly engaged; the other Ospreys, who were left behind when Wil and Melanie entered the Indigo Kingdom palace; and Black Knife.<br /></p><p>RELATIONSHIPS<br /></p><p>Can I just say oh my, Black Knife? That is one masked vigilante I wouldn’t mind being captured by. Of course, in the sample I read, which is only about one-third of the book, Wil and Black Knife aren’t friends yet, but are becoming uneasy, if still suspicious, allies. I’m certain I know his true identity – it’s a bit hard to write this kind of Young Adult novel without being all obvious about it – and I’d really like to see Wil realise it, too, and then get on with the kissing. I mean, there’s nothing romantic between them in the sample, but I just know it’s got to work out that way. Why else were we introduced so early? It’s the basis of YA!<br /></p><p>I am aware of another book with a similar theme I recently read, Sarah Raasch’s Snow Like Ashes. Both contain young women leads who are capable warriors, who are <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[rightful heirs <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> from kingdoms that have been enslaved by a neighbour due to a policy on magic use. Why did I rate the sample of The Orphan Queen 5 stars and Snow Like Ashes, which I read in its entirely only 4, if they are so similar and both enjoyable? It’s as simple as this: I didn’t feel the romance at all in Snow Like Ashes, and although there was not yet any romance written into The Orphan Queen, I could have cut the sexual tension with a knife.<br /></p><p>OVERALL<br /></p><p>I need the rest of this book right now. Like, RIGHT NOW. And I'll probably track down Meadows' Incarnate books as well, because I just really enjoyed reading this sample of The Orphan Queen.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="16681263153355731511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1662477799" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1662477799" />
    <a title="Sarah (thegirltheycalljones)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32607699-sarah-thegirltheycalljones"><img alt="Sarah (thegirltheycalljones)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569607878p2/32607699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1662477799?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah (thegirltheycalljones)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah (thegirltheycalljones)" href="/user/show/32607699-sarah-thegirltheycalljones">Sarah (thegirltheycalljones)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32607699-sarah-thegirltheycalljones?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1662477799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10370571561226482882">DNFed around 57%.<br/><br/>I tried to hold on as long as I could but I'm totally unable to finish this one.<br/>I'm sure it's an okay book if you haven't already read a fuckton of fantasy YA about a magical princess/queen in hiding, planning to recapture her realm from the Big Bad Usurper (who's probably not that bad, because our MC doesn't know shit about what happened after all).<br/>I tried to care. I tried <i>very hard</i>. But I didn't.<br/><br/>Wil, our MC, is very inconstant. I don't understand wat the author tried to do wit</span>
  <span id="freeText10370571561226482882" style="display:none">DNFed around 57%.<br /><br />I tried to hold on as long as I could but I'm totally unable to finish this one.<br />I'm sure it's an okay book if you haven't already read a fuckton of fantasy YA about a magical princess/queen in hiding, planning to recapture her realm from the Big Bad Usurper (who's probably not that bad, because our MC doesn't know shit about what happened after all).<br />I tried to care. I tried <i>very hard</i>. But I didn't.<br /><br />Wil, our MC, is very inconstant. I don't understand wat the author tried to do with her. One page she's all combative and defiant, and the next she's whiny and overwhelmed with emotions.<br />The fact that she "couldn't breathe", "couldn't speak anymore", was "choking" <i>every time</i> somebody talked about her fallen kingdom was very irritating.<br />See, Wil was an undercover spy, posing as a random noble in the Big Bad Usurper castle in order to overthrow the current king. <br />The fact that she was so lame at her spy job was exasperating. She constantly had a weird attitude, jeopardizing the mission - but in theory only! She acted crap in public but we were <i>told</i> she was successfully doing a lot of spy stuff without ever showing it to us! All her actions were summed up in a few lines like "yesterday, I searched all the offices and I found nothing". <br />Oh, okay then. Better get back to the suitors parade!<br />In order to avoid spoilers, I'll stay very vague, because we got a masked man in the lot, which identity was not yet revealed when I stopped reading (but you don't have to graduate from an Ivy League school to guess who that dude could be...).<br />So we had the prince, the prince guard and the vigilante, also known as Boring, Cliché and Kinda Hot. I have nothing to add.<br />Also, it was <b>completely implausible</b> that Wil didn't guess who the masked man was.<br />But again, I DNFed the book so maybe we get a good explanation later.<br /><br />The other characters were meh. <br />I liked that Wil couldn't trust her team, that changed a bit. Melanie and Patrick were not very reliable and their intentions were not clear, it was an interesting premise to surround the MC with multi layered characters.<br />But the result was average. Their dialogues were more irritating than interesting and the suspense was not handled very well. Everything was guessable from a gazillion miles.<br />But again, I DNFed the book so maybe we get a good explanation later.<br /><br />The story was not original. Same old song "I lost my kingdom, I want it back" and "magic exists but we're not allowed to use it". Zzzzz. I mean, at least SJM gives us <s>smut</s> steam. Kinda. <br />But again, I DNFed the book so maybe we get a good explanation later.<br /><br />I kept reading for the masked man (cf. nickname given above - and you know it can't be good when you're holding on just for the sake of a hot dude) but he was definitely not enough to get me to the end. <br />I'll gladly read something else now, preferably a good book without lost princesses.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10370571561226482882" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1277556503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1277556503" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1277556503?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=fantasy-all">fantasy-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1277556503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6972687927749266812"> MY BLOG: <a href='http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2015/12/the-orphan-queen-by-jodi-meadows.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448912596i/17205490._SX540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>When I first started this book, I couldn't get into it, it was slow, or maybe it was just my reading slump. Who knows, at any rate after I got back into reading it I enjoyed it. After a bit it picks up and is a really good story. <br/><br/>Wilhemina (Wil) is the orphan queen of Aecor. Her parents were killed many years ago during the 'One Night War' Wil and a bunch of other kids were taken to an orphanage. The Aecor kingdom is now watched over by some jerk. Anyway, a</span>
  <span id="freeText6972687927749266812" style="display:none"> MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2015/12/the-orphan-queen-by-jodi-meadows.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448912596i/17205490._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When I first started this book, I couldn't get into it, it was slow, or maybe it was just my reading slump. Who knows, at any rate after I got back into reading it I enjoyed it. After a bit it picks up and is a really good story. <br><br>Wilhemina (Wil) is the orphan queen of Aecor. Her parents were killed many years ago during the 'One Night War' Wil and a bunch of other kids were taken to an orphanage. The Aecor kingdom is now watched over by some jerk. Anyway, a guy named Patrick, who is the leader of the Osprey's, rescues all of the kids and they join his group. They are all trying to get Wil back to Aecor and make the kingdom prosper again. But, not all is as it seems in this group..... <br><br>Here's a real Osprey if you interested ↓ He/she says hello! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450618836i/17449241.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Soooo... those that do magic can't do it any more because it has been banned. The reason for that is that the magic creates wraith, it's called a toxic by-product. What it does it gets into people and animals and mutates them. They are evil and try to kill everything when that happens. They have glow men, gargantuan cats, insects.. you get the picture. They can transform into whatever in some cases. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450618836i/17449242.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There is a guy that runs around in a mask killing the wraiths and taking anyone that uses magic to the police. People call him Black Knife. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450618836i/17449243.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Black Knife is trying to figure out Wil and her band of merry men and women to see if they are thieves or use magic... etc.. <br><br>Wil has magic by the way and uses it every now and again. <br><br>Wil and her best friend Melanie, that is in the Osprey group too, plant themselves in the Palace acting like other noble women from another kingdom. This happens to be where the king that killed Wil's parents lives. Isn't life grand. But not all is as it seems of course. Oh and his son is there as well and she doesn't like him either. <br><br>Anyhoo.... Patrick is the leader of the Osprey's and he turns into a big ole jerk, trust me. <br><br>Wil starts going out on missions with Black Knife, yeah, they become friends and then fall in love.. isn't that sweet and they kill wraiths together and save people on the streets. Well all of that sweetness goes away when we find out who Black Knife really is.. that's always the case.. well mostly anyway. <br><br>The ending of the book was like.. um.. cliffhanger like that... really? Of course now I'm going to have to read the next book as I have a fondness for Will and Black Knife now. I like people that have bad arseness in them :) <br><br>I'm glad I pushed on through the book because it did turn out really good for me. I try to do that because a lot of times that is the case. <br><br>Fin <br><br></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('J868hUbiGOhZsvuDVkqgpE2cZ4dfmQpiMJEHpPuiLJ1JA/36peNznY6Z4Zkgjb3xUd8F7CHKOBv/0SDFUsuTmg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QFniC4EellI1+lQfg6gQvyiMxAiTlBeFXEb17m+hSOAulKN0Yh/9J+LRTgX1bw3qNM+mY+3HJfyTBtKPxsj35w==')})
  }
//]]>
